    [Original] Made Fresh Salads, Inc. Recalls Assorted Flavors of Cream Cheese Because of Possible Health Risk
    More Recalls, Market Withdrawals, & Safety Alerts Made Fresh Salads, Inc. of Bay Shore, NY is recalling assorted flavors of cream cheese because they have the potential to be contaminated with Listeria monocytogenes, an organism which can cause serious and sometimes fatal infections in young children, frail or elderly people, and others with weakened immune systems. Although healthy individuals may suffer only short-term symptoms such as high fever, severe headache, stiffness, nausea, abdominal pain and diarrhea, Listeria infection can cause miscarriages and stillbirths among pregnant women. The cream cheese was distributed in Brooklyn, Queens, Bronx and New York City area by direct delivery to retail stores and distributors. Products are distributed in 5 lb. white plastic tubs with a Made Fresh Salads label. The flavors being recalled are as follows with expiration dates through February 27, 2026, marked in the bottom left corner of the label. 5 lb. tub Apple Cinnamon Cream Cheese5 lb. tub Caramel Apple Cream Cheese5 lb. tub Blueberry Cream Cheese5 lb. tub Garlic & Herb Cream Cheese5 lb. tub Jalapeno Cream Cheese5 lb. tub Jalapeno Cheddar Cream Cheese5 lb. tub Lox Cream Cheese5 lb. tub Scallion Cream Cheese5 lb. tub Strawberry Cream Cheese5 lb. tub Sundried Tomato Cream Cheese5 lb. tub Vegetable Cream Cheese5 lb. tub Walnut Raisin Cream Cheese5 lb. tub Whipped Cream Cheese5 lb. tub Tofu Whipped The recall was the result of a routine sampling program by the company which revealed that a part of the mixer used to manufacture finished products was contaminated with Listeria monocytogenes. The company has ceased production using the mixer in question and removed it from service. Consumers who have purchased Made Fresh Salads cream cheese are urged to return it to the place of purchase for a full refund. Consumers with questions may contact the company at 1-718-765-0082 Monday through Friday 9am to 5pm ET.

    [Original] Why fake AI videos of UK urban decline are taking over social media
    An AI-generated video depicting a crowd of young, mostly Black men in balaclavas and padded jackets sliding into a filthy Croydon swimming pool has gone viral, part of a growing trend of deepfakes portraying Western cities like London, Manchester, and San Francisco as overrun by crime and immigrationâ€”labeled â€œdecline porn.â€ The video, created by a content creator using the handle RadialB, claims to show a taxpayer-funded facility, though RadialB, a 20-something from north-west England, has never visited Croydon. Some videos include disclaimers stating they are AI-generated, complying with TikTok, Instagram, and X policies, yet many viewers still believe them real. RadialB admits his content provokes political reactions, including racist comments, though he claims platforms filter such abuse. Critics, including a Croydon-based Black TikToker named C.Tino, argue the videos falsely depict their neighborhoods as â€œghetto.â€ The trend has spread globally, with accounts from Israel, Brazil, and the Middle East sharing similar content. Some fake news accounts on TikTok purport to be British media, amplifying negative narratives.     In Mason County, Michigan, a growing resistance is emerging as tech companies pursue vast datacenter projects on rural farmland, offering multimillion-dollar deals that many farmers are refusing.     [Original] Humans vs robots? China begs to disagree
    As China embraces humanoid robots, policymakers and companies are expanding the scope of innovation and applications in daily life The 2026 Spring Festival Gala, one of the worldâ€™s most-watched television events, featured a dazzling array of humanoid robots. They performed martial arts, executed intricate sword dances and even took part in a comedy skit alongside human celebrities.While parts of the world still view humanoid robots with a mixture of fear and suspicion, as potential job-stealers or sci-fi villains, China is increasingly embracing them as partners in work, entertainment and daily life. Amid the escalating artificial intelligence (AI) race, China is not just competing on technological prowess but is rapidly outpacing others in its willingness to integrate these machines into public life.China accounted for 90 per cent of the roughly 13,000 humanoid robots shipped globally last year. The country also represented over half of the humanoid robot exhibitors at the Consumer Electronics Show 2026. This burgeoning ecosystem draws researchers, engineers, entrepreneurs and investors into a fast-growing market.AdvertisementIt is fuelled by a parallel explosion in large language models and multi-modal AI, from ByteDanceâ€™s Doubao to the DeepSeek and Qwen models. Such AI models help robots understand user requests, engage in conversation, analyse data and provide useful content. As more robots are deployed in the physical world, the AI models are enhanced by the influx of real-world data, which in turn intensifies competition in large language models themselves and further encourages innovation.The gala offered a stunning showcase of this progress. Robots from companies like Unitree, Galbot and Noetix ran, danced and performed acrobatics on stage. One might dismiss a backflipping robot, clad in a Monkey King costume, as a spectacle. But the nimbleness of the arms, legs, waist, neck, ankles and fingers shows technological breakthroughs.

    [Original] æ¸…åAIRå›¢é˜Ÿæ­ç¤ºäººç±»ä¸æ™ºé©¾ç®—æ³•è§†è§‰æ³¨æ„åŠ›çš„æœ¬è´¨å·®å¼‚
    On February 21, according to the Institute for AI Research at Tsinghua University, the AIR team from Tsinghua University has published a study titled "Human and Algorithmic Visual Attention in Driving Tasks" in npj Artificial Intelligence in February 2026. Using autonomous drivingâ€”a safety-critical domainâ€”as a platform, the study for the first time systematically dissects the fundamental differences between human and algorithmic visual attention through a dual-track design combining "human eye-tracking experiments" and "algorithmic comparative validation." Its core contribution lies in proposing a three-stage quantitative framework for human driving attention. The study confirms that the fundamental limitation of algorithmic visual understanding is the lack of "semantic saliency extraction capability." Integrating human inspection-stage semantic attention can effectively bridge the "semantic gap" in specialized algorithms and the "grounding gap" in large models in an economical and efficient manner, without relying on large-scale pre-training.

    [Original] MPs to discuss inquiry into trade envoy role after Andrew arrest
    The UKâ€™s Business and Trade Committee will meet to discuss launching an inquiry into the role of trade envoys following the arrest of Andrew Mountbatten-Windsor, a former royal, by Thames Valley Police on suspicion of misconduct in public office.     [Original] Trumpâ€™s Trade Gamble Will Continue, Despite Supreme Court Rebuke
    The Supreme Court ruled 6-3 against President Trumpâ€™s use of an international emergency law to impose tariffs, but Trump vowed to continue his tariff policy, claiming â€œnumerous other waysâ€ exist to maintain or increase levies. At a White House news conference, he asserted that tariffs had â€œbroken every record in the bookâ€ and promised a new 10% across-the-board tariff, later raising it to 15%â€”the maximum allowed under a new legal provision. He announced via Truth Social that the administration would issue new, legally permissible tariffs in the coming months, citing Section 122 of the 1974 Trade Act, which addresses balance of payments deficits rather than trade deficits. Critics argue this rationale is flawed, as the two metrics differ significantly. Trump frames tariffs as a remedy to globalization, aiming to bring manufacturing back to the U.S., reduce reliance on foreign goods, and shrink the trade deficit. However, data contradicts his claims. The annual goods trade deficit hit a record high in 2025, and while the deficit with China narrowed due to a nearly 30% drop in imports, U.S. exports to Chinaâ€”including soybeansâ€”also declined. Imports from Vietnam, Mexico, India, and other nations reached record levels, indicating trade was merely reshuffled, not reduced. Despite a strong overall economy, manufacturing gains have been concentrated in sectors like electronics and aerospaceâ€”less affected by tariffsâ€”while auto manufacturers and others face challenges. Manufacturing output growth has not translated into job creation; American factories cut over 80,000 jobs in the past year. Trump has dismissed contradictory data, claiming on Truth Social that the trade deficit had â€œBEEN REDUCED BY 78%â€ and would turn positive â€œfor the first time in many decadesâ€â€”a claim unsupported by official statistics. The brief dip in the trade deficit in October 2024 was driven by volatile factors, including gold and pharmaceutical trade fluctuations and pre-tariff stockpiling, not structural change. Imports rebounded in November and December, fueled by semiconductorsâ€”exempt from tariffs due to their role in AI-driven economic growth. Economists like Brad W. Setser note that tariffs could reduce the trade deficit by slowing economic growth and consumption, but only if the revenue is used to shrink the government deficit. However, exemptions for key goods like electronics and pharmaceuticals have limited the policyâ€™s impact. Ultimately, tariffs have not revitalized U.S. manufacturing or meaningfully altered the trade deficit, according to Setser. The future remains uncertain, with the 150-day tariff plan requiring congressional approval or replacement. One thing is clear: Trumpâ€™s tariffs have not resolved the â€œemergencyâ€ he claimed they were designed to address.

    [Original] Inside the Big Tech Lobbying Machine Aiming to Halt Social Media Bans
    American tech giants, including Meta and Google, are intensifying lobbying efforts in Europe amid growing momentum for teen social media bans. In November, Dutch Green Party lawmaker Kim van Sparrentak was startled to hear a Meta ad opposing a proposed ban on social media for teenagers while listening to a podcastâ€”highlighting the industryâ€™s aggressive, multi-channel campaign. The companies are pushing back against legislation in France, Germany, Spain, Britain, Denmark, and Australia, where a ban for under-16s took effect in December. Eight U.S. states have also introduced similar measures. The core of the tech industryâ€™s strategy is to replace outright bans with alternatives like a â€œdigital majority age,â€ requiring parental approval for teens under 15 or 16 to access platforms. Meta promotes its 2024 â€œteen accounts,â€ which grant parents control over content visibility. Companies argue that bans could drive youth to unregulated parts of the internet and are difficult to enforce. French National Assembly member Laure Miller countered that enforcement challenges should not deter action, citing the highway code as a precedent. Brussels has become the epicenter of this lobbying battle. In 2024, tech firms spent â‚¬151 million ($178 million) on E.U. lobbyingâ€”up over 55% since 2021â€”making Meta the top spender at â‚¬10 million and Google â‚¬4.5 million. There are now 890 full-time tech lobbyists in Brussels, surpassing the number of European Parliament members. The industry is also courting far-right MEPs, with Meta holding 38 meetings with them between July 2024 and December 2025. High-profile campaigns include billboards in Brussels stations featuring historical figures like Gutenberg and Marconi, warning that modern regulations could stifle innovation. Meta also ran a full-page ad in European newspapers, signed by global safety head Antigone Davis, advocating for a digital majority age. The European Commission is currently consulting on whether to adopt this alternative instead of a ban. The Digital Fairness Act, expected to be voted on late this year, would ban features like infinite scrolling, autoplay, and engagement-based recommendationsâ€”requiring major platform redesigns. â€œWeâ€™re working like crazy on it,â€ said Isabelle PÃ©rignon, consumer policy director at the European Commission. The outcome in Brussels could shape global policy, including in the U.S.

    [Original] For India, Buying Russian Oil Just Got More Complicated
    The U.S. Supreme Courtâ€™s recent ruling invalidating President Trumpâ€™s use of the International Emergency Economic Powers Act has created political and economic turbulence for India, particularly for Prime Minister Narendra Modi. Just weeks after India secured a trade deal that lifted a 50% tariff on its exports, the courtâ€™s decision undermines the legal basis for the punitive measure that had pressured India to cut Russian oil imports. The Trump administration had framed the tariff relief as a quid pro quo for Indiaâ€™s pledge to stop buying Russian crude, a condition reiterated in a White House document dated February 9. However, Indian buyers had already been reducing Russian oil purchases for months, driven in part by U.S. Treasury sanctions on Rosneft and Lukoil starting in October. Indiaâ€™s government has consistently maintained that its decisions were guided by â€œnational interests,â€ avoiding acknowledgment of direct U.S. coercion. Foreign Ministry spokesman Randhir Jaiswal said the February 9 document was â€œconsistentâ€ with prior agreements, but offered no further clarification after the ruling. Russia has dismissed claims of a policy shift, with its foreign ministry stating on February 18 that Indiaâ€™s position on Russian hydrocarbons remains unchanged. Despite the deal, Indiaâ€™s agricultural market liberalization and a pledge to spend $500 billion on U.S. goods over five years have drawn fierce criticism from farmers and opposition parties, who view the agreement as a capitulation. The Supreme Courtâ€™s ruling now casts doubt on the dealâ€™s foundation, prompting Indiaâ€™s main opposition party to call for its suspension. Yet, strategic alignment remains intact: on the same day as the ruling, U.S. Ambassador Sergio Gor welcomed Indiaâ€™s entry into the Pax Silica initiative, a Trump-era program aimed at building China-independent supply chains in critical minerals and semiconductors. The initiative, now involving 12 countries, resonates with Indiaâ€™s strategic concerns, especially after a 2017 border clash with China. Despite this, the political cost of reversing course on Russian oilâ€”where Indian refiners still imported about one million barrels per day in February, according to Kpler dataâ€”remains high. Analyst Muyu Xu noted that while Indian refiners are shifting suppliers, it may take another month to confirm whether Russian crude flows are being fully curtailed. With the legal justification for the original pressure now void, Modi faces mounting scrutiny over whether to uphold or revise the deal, balancing U.S. strategic interests against domestic political fallout.

    Aritzia Inc., the Canadian fashion retailer known for its accessible luxury aesthetic, has acquired Fred Segal from the Segal family, reviving the iconic Los Angeles brand. The deal includes a lease agreement to reopen a Fred Segal store at 8100 Melrose Avenue, the site of the original flagship that opened in the 1960s and closed in 2017. It gained fame for its curation of emerging designers, including Kate Spade, J Brand, Juicy Couture, Dries Van Noten, and Maison Margiela, and attracted celebrities such as Diana Ross, Lenny Kravitz, Paris Hilton, and Kendall Jenner.     [Original] Trump says he's considering limited military strike against Iran
    President Donald Trump said Friday that he is considering limited military strikes to pressure Iran over its nuclear program. "I guess I can say I am considering that," Trump said when asked by a reporter at a White House breakfast with U.S. governors. Trump said Thursday that he would make a decision in the next 10 to 15 days on whether to attack the Islamic Republic. He has left open the possibility that a deal could still be reached with Tehran over its nuclear program. Trump has previously said an attack on Iran would be "far worse" than the limited strikes launched by the U.S. in June against its nuclear facilities. Oil prices were stable Friday after rallying more than 5% this week as traders price in some risk of imminent U.S. military action. U.S. crude oil fell 4 cents to close at $66.39 per barrel. Global benchmark Brent rose 10 cents to settle at $71.76 per barrel. A massive U.S. military buildup is underway in the Middle East. The USS Abraham Lincoln aircraft carrier is in the region. A second aircraft carrier, the USS Gerald Ford, is en route. The oil market's biggest fear is that a conflict between the U.S. and Iran could lead to a prolonged disruption of oil flows through the Strait of Hormuz. The strait is a vital chokepoint for the global oil trade. More than 14 million barrels per day of oil and condensates passed through the narrow waterway on average in 2025, according to data from consulting firm Kpler, which says that amount accounts for a third of total worldwide seaborne oil exports. About three-quarters of the oil that passes through the strait goes to China, India, Japan and South Korea, according to Kpler.

    [Original] Market volatility trap? Why this income-first strategy may 'leave a lot on the table'
    The market volatility may be leading retail investors astray. According to Kathmere Capital Management's Nick Ryder, they shouldn't use the current backdrop as an excuse to dive into defensive trades â€” including dividend-paying stocks and bonds. "Oftentimes, we just see too often people taking an income-focused approach, and it leaves a lot on the table," the firm's chief investment officer told CNBC's "ETF Edge" this week. "We generally just advise for all of our clients to take a total return-oriented approach â€¦ that's going to apply across stocks, bonds and everything in between within a portfolio." Ryder, whose firm has $3.5 billion in assets under management, warns against so-called "yield-chasing." "Within fixed income, it could be yield-chasing in terms of moving further out interest rate risk, taking greater amounts of duration and portfolio, [and] moving from investment grade to high-yield bonds â€”which have dramatically different risk and return expectations," he added. Ryder contends income shouldn't be the foundation of long-term portfolios. He indicates investors are better served starting with goals and risk tolerance, then adding income, because pullbacks are part of long-term investing. An income-first approach, he cautions, can quietly push portfolios into unintended bets. He's also optimistic about the macro backdrop. "Overall, the economy has been pretty darn resilient," added Ryder. "You've seen corporate profitability be very resilient." That total-return approach is also why Amplify ETFs' Christian Magoon is urging investors not to let the distribution number drive the decisions. "We think being smart about yield means balancing attractive yield with upside or long-term capital appreciation â€¦ not just going for a maximum possible yield," the firm's CEO said in the same interview. "We think that's a yield trap."

    [Original] Killing of nationalist student leaves French far left in deep trouble as elections loom
    The killing of nationalist student Quentin Deranque in Lyon on 12 February has triggered a seismic shift in Franceâ€™s political landscape, raising questions about whether the far left is supplanting the far right as the pariah of French politics. Deranque, a far-right feminist supporter, was fatally attacked by masked, hooded youths during a protest, with mobile phone footage showing him repeatedly kicked and punched. He died from head injuries. Seven suspects have been charged, all linked to La Jeune Garde (The Young Guard), a group previously tied to La France Insoumise (LFI), the radical left party led by Jean-Luc MÃ©lenchon, which holds 70 seats in the 577-member National Assembly. One suspect, Jacques-Elie Favrot, was a salaried assistant to LFI deputy RaphaÃ«l Arnault, who founded The Young Guard in 2018. Favrot faces charges of â€œcomplicity to murder by instigation,â€ while Adrian Besseyre, another suspect, is charged with murder. All deny intent to kill, though some admitted being present and delivering blows. The incident has sparked widespread condemnation of LFI, with traditionalist, Catholic, nationalist, and neo-fascist groups holding a 3,000-person rally in Lyon, while the National Rally (RN), Franceâ€™s largest party, stayed away. For decades, the RN was the party ostracized due to its extremist past, but now, with LFI implicated in violence, the political balance is shifting. The RN, under Marine Le Pen and Jordan Bardella, has long pursued a â€œde-demonisationâ€ strategy, and Deranqueâ€™s death has accelerated it. The cordon sanitaireâ€”coalitions to block the RNâ€”has relied on cooperation with LFI, which was considered part of the â€œRepublican arc.â€ But if mainstream parties like the Socialists (70 MPs) and centrists (160 MPs) now refuse to ally with LFI, the anti-RN coalition could collapse. Commentators like Guillaume Tabard of Le Figaro argue that LFI has become the most condemned political force, while the RN benefits from the shift. LFIâ€™s refusal to condemn The Young Guard or suspend Arnault has deepened the crisis. Former prime minister Dominique de Villepin warned that focusing attacks on LFI creates a â€œcorridor of respectabilityâ€ for the RN, offering it the â€œappearance of normalityâ€ it has long sought. The implications are profound, especially ahead of 2027 presidential and parliamentary elections, and could reshape Franceâ€™s political future.

    [Original] Giant tortoises return to GalÃ¡pagos island after nearly 200 years
    ShareSaveJessica RawnsleyShareSaveWatch: Giant tortoises return to GalÃ¡pagos island after nearly 200 yearsGiant tortoises are roaming the GalÃ¡pagos island of Floreana for the first time in more than 180 years, in what conservationists have called a "hugely significant milestone". The release of 158 captive-bred juvenile tortoises onto the island is part of the Floreana Ecological Restoration Project led by the GalÃ¡pagos National Park Directorate. The reintroduction follows a "back-breeding" programme launched in 2017 after scientists discovered tortoises carrying ancestry of the Floreana giant tortoise on nearby Isabela island. Floreana's native species, Chelonoidis niger niger, was driven to extinction in the 1840s by sailors who took thousands from the island for sustenance during long voyages. "The restoration of Floreana has reached a hugely significant milestone, with 158 captive-bred giant tortoises released into the wild this week," the GalÃ¡pagos Conservation Trust (GCT) said in a statement on Friday. "This long-anticipated moment gives hope, not just for the future of Floreana, but for the future restoration of islands around the world," it added. Dr Jen Jones, GCT chief executive, described the moment as "truly spine-tingling," adding that it had validated two decades of collaboration between scientists, charities and the local community. The conservation project became possible after scientists discovered tortoises carrying Floreana ancestry on Wolf Volcano on Isabela island in 2008. Researchers selected 23 hybrid tortoises with the closest genetic links to the extinct subspecies and began breeding them in captivity on Santa Cruz island. By 2025, more than 600 hatchlings had been produced, with several hundred now large enough to survive in the wild. The GCT described the giant tortoises as "ecosystem engineers" and said they played an "outsized role in restoring degraded ecosystems" because of the way their activity shapes landscapes.

    [Original] Anna Murdoch-Mann, writer and former News Corp director, dies aged 81
    ShareSaveOttilie MitchellShareSaveRon Galella Collection via Getty ImagesAnna Murdoch-Mann, writer and ex-wife of media baron Rupert Murdoch, has died aged 81, his media outlets have announced. Married to the media mogul for 31 years, she played an influential role on the board of his publishing giant, News Corp. She was mother to three of Murdoch's children, Elisabeth, James, and Lachlan Murdoch - who is now chairman of Fox and News Corp - and stepmother to his daughter, Prudence. Murdoch-Mann, who was also a philanthropist, died on 17 February "surrounded by family" at her home in Palm Beach, Florida. Born Anna Torv in Glasgow and raised as a Catholic, she moved to Australia aged nine. After her parents' divorce, she is said to have brought up her own siblings. She became a reporter for the Sydney Daily Telegraph and the Sydney Daily Mirror, where she met Rupert Murdoch and went on to serve on the board of his company. "He never made a major business decision without her input", The Australian, another title in his media stable, writes. She penned several novels during their marriage, including the 1988 Family Business about a multi-generational media dynasty. The couple moved to London, where in 1969 a woman was abducted and held to ransom in Hertfordshire - mistaken for Murdoch-Mann. Muriel McKay was killed by her kidnappers and there have been renewed efforts to find her body in recent years. The then-Murdochs divorced in 1999 in one of the most expensive separations in history - Murdoch-Mann received a $1.7bn (Â£1bn) settlement. Murdoch married his third wife, Wendi Deng, 17 days later. In an exclusive interview after her separation, Murdoch-Mann told Australian Women's Weekly, "I think there's going to be a lot of heartbreak and hardship" over the succession for Murdoch's media empire. "There's been such a lot of pressure that they needn't have had at their age," she added. These tensions inspired the television series Succession and played out in courts in real life too. A years-long court battle ended with Murdoch's eldest son, Lachlan, being set to control the news group late last year. Murdoch-Mann went on to remarry, first to financier William Mann, who died in 2017. She later wed her third husband, Ashton dePeyster, who survives her along with 10 grandchildren and one great-grandchild. The philanthropist served on the boards of several children's hospitals including in Los Angeles and Haiti. In 1998, she was made a Dame of the Order of St Gregory by Pope John Paul II.

    [Original] Katseye's Manon to take 'temporary hiatus' to focus on health
    ShareSaveJessica RawnsleyShareSaveGetty ImagesKatseye performed at the 2026 Grammy Awards, where they were nominated for best new artistKatseye member Manon Bannerman is taking a temporary break to focus on her health and wellbeing, the group has announced. The 23-year-old Swiss singer told fans she was "healthy" and "taking care of myself," adding: "Sometimes things unfold in ways we don't fully control, but I'm trusting the bigger picture." The six-member girl group, formed in 2023, said the decision had been made following "open and thoughtful conversations together". The announcement comes weeks after Katseye performed at the Grammy Awards in Los Angeles, where they were nominated for best new artist and best pop duo/group performance for their song, Gabriela. "Thank you for standing by me," Bannerman wrote on Katseye's WeVerse fandom page on Friday. "I love you endlessly and can't wait to see you again." In a statement on WeVerse shared by their label, HYBE and Geffen Records, the group said: "We fully support this decision. Katseye remains committed to showing up for one another and for the fans who mean everything to us." Katseye confirmed they would continue scheduled performances during Bannerman's absence and "look forward to being together again when the time is right". No timeline has been given for her return. The group - which also includes Daniela Avanzini, Lara Raj, Megan Skiendiel, Sophia Laforteza and Yoonchae Jeung - was formed during the 2023 reality competition series The Debut: Dream Academy. They released their first single in June 2024 with the song Debut and have since released two EPs, SIS (Soft is Strong) and Beautiful Chaos, alongside a string of singles. The group has previously spoken about the pressures of their rapid global rise to fame and the online scrutiny that has accompanied it. Last year the girl group said they had received thousands of death threats since the band was formed. "I try to tell myself it doesn't matter, but if 1,000 people are sending you death threats, it's jarring," Lara Raj told the BBC. Raj said people see the band as "women to rank," calling it "so dystopian". Bannerman added that it was "very terrorising on the mind".

    [Original] Venezuela receives more than 1,500 amnesty requests under new law
    More than 1,550 political prisoners in Venezuela have applied for amnesty under a newly enacted law, with 80 already released, according to National Assembly chief Jorge Rodriguez. The amnesty law, unanimously approved by the legislature two days prior, allows for conditional release but requires individual petitions to the courts handling each case. Prosecutors have requested the release of 379 individuals, including opposition members, activists, human rights defenders, and journalists detained for months or years. Most of those freed so far were held in Caracas, with further releases expected within 15 days, said Jorge Arreaza, the lawmaker overseeing the process. The law was championed by interim President Delcy Rodriguez, sister of the National Assembly leader, following the U.S.-backed military raid on January 3 that resulted in the abduction of former President NicolÃ¡s Maduro. Maduro and his wife are now in U.S. custody awaiting trial on drug trafficking charges, with Maduro pleading not guilty and claiming he is a â€œprisoner of war.â€ Rodriguez stated the law marked a shift toward â€œletting go of a little intoleranceâ€ and opening new political avenues. However, critics argue the law is discriminatory and unconstitutional. Human rights group Foro Penalâ€™s president, Alfredo Romero, condemned the exclusion of military personnel and persecuted political figures, asserting that true national coexistence is impossible without their inclusion. The law explicitly excludes those prosecuted for â€œpromotingâ€ or â€œfacilitatingâ€¦ armed or forceful actionsâ€ against Venezuelaâ€™s sovereignty by foreign actorsâ€”charges previously used against opposition leader Maria Corina Machado, a Nobel Peace Prize laureate currently in the U.S. Juan Pablo Guanipa, a close ally of Machado, had his house arrest lifted, his brother, lawmaker Tomas Guanipa, confirmed to Reuters. Additionally, members of the security forces convicted of â€œterrorismâ€-related activities are not covered. However, the law does extend to 11,000 individuals previously paroled or under house arrest over nearly three decades, allowing their substitute measures to be lifted and enabling full freedom. Outside Caracasâ€™s Zone 7 police facility, relatives of detaineesâ€”some camped for weeksâ€”awaited news. â€œLetâ€™s hope itâ€™s true,â€ said Genesis Rojas. A group chanted, â€œWe want to go home!â€ Hundreds have already been conditionally released since the January 3 raid, which triggered widespread political upheaval.

    [Original] Humans vs robots? China begs to disagree
    As China embraces humanoid robots, policymakers and companies are expanding the scope of innovation and applications in daily life The 2026 Spring Festival Gala, one of the worldâ€™s most-watched television events, featured a dazzling array of humanoid robots. They performed martial arts, executed intricate sword dances and even took part in a comedy skit alongside human celebrities.While parts of the world still view humanoid robots with a mixture of fear and suspicion, as potential job-stealers or sci-fi villains, China is increasingly embracing them as partners in work, entertainment and daily life. Amid the escalating artificial intelligence (AI) race, China is not just competing on technological prowess but is rapidly outpacing others in its willingness to integrate these machines into public life.China accounted for 90 per cent of the roughly 13,000 humanoid robots shipped globally last year. The country also represented over half of the humanoid robot exhibitors at the Consumer Electronics Show 2026. This burgeoning ecosystem draws researchers, engineers, entrepreneurs and investors into a fast-growing market.AdvertisementIt is fuelled by a parallel explosion in large language models and multi-modal AI, from ByteDanceâ€™s Doubao to the DeepSeek and Qwen models. Such AI models help robots understand user requests, engage in conversation, analyse data and provide useful content. As more robots are deployed in the physical world, the AI models are enhanced by the influx of real-world data, which in turn intensifies competition in large language models themselves and further encourages innovation.The gala offered a stunning showcase of this progress. Robots from companies like Unitree, Galbot and Noetix ran, danced and performed acrobatics on stage. One might dismiss a backflipping robot, clad in a Monkey King costume, as a spectacle. But the nimbleness of the arms, legs, waist, neck, ankles and fingers shows technological breakthroughs.

    [Original] The rail ahead: as high-speed lines saturate China, how far can their global reach extend?
    As Chinese giants eye Eurasia for new infrastructure, analysts speculate on what it will take to keep overseas projects from going off the rails in different host nations Chinese railway giants look set to scout Eurasia in the years ahead to build high-speed train lines as the domestic market matures and some countries are more prepared than others for capital-intensive yet transformative ventures, analysts said. Inspired by China-invested projects such as the 142km (88-mile) Jakarta-Bandung high-speed line in Indonesia and the partly finished 350km (217-mile) Budapest-Belgrade railway, Chinese construction and engineering firms are expected to expand their overseas footprint. Projects abroad are now more crucial as giant domestic railway engineering firms, builders and operators are finding diminishing new ground to break in China, especially in cities. â€œLike any engineering firms anywhere, theyâ€™ll be looking for new opportunities, but the fiscal positions of governments around the region will have to be quite careful in terms of how they spend money,â€ said Song Seng Wun, an economic adviser at Singapore-based fintech firm SDAX. Analysts point to Southeast Asian countries such as Laos, Malaysia and Thailand as the most likely future destinations for Chinese-invested high-speed projects, with Central Asia not far behind as it leverages existing trade-linked infrastructure that China has already helped build there.

    [Original] How the next China shock is shaping hearts and minds
    No longer confined to trade and technology, competition between China and the West is now playing out in the realm of cultural imagination For decades, Chinaâ€™s role in the global economy was easy to define. It made things cheaply and at astonishing scale. â€œMade in Chinaâ€ became shorthand for industrial capacity. It was often contentious, sometimes admired, sometimes feared. That division is now eroding. In smartphones, electric vehicles (EVs) and digital services, Chinese firms are climbing the value chain, competing with Western companies and, in many sectors, leading globally. But the next China shock may take a different form. Call it China Shock 2.0 or 3.0, depending on how you count them, but China is no longer just manufacturing the worldâ€™s products. It is increasingly manufacturing the worldâ€™s preferences, too. Especially among younger consumers, Chinese brands are shaping tastes, aesthetics and the global image of China. Geopolitically, this shift matters. Competition between China and the West is no longer confined to trade and technology. It is increasingly playing out in the realm of cultural imagination. If tariffs and export controls are tools of hard power rivalry, brands are tools of soft power. The question is how to compete with China in the latter arena.

    [Original] ç”·å­è‡ªé©¾æ¸¸å¼€10å°æ—¶åå¼ƒè½¦æ¢é«˜é“
    Recently, a man who completed a 10-hour self-driving journey from Chengdu, Sichuan Province, to Dali, Yunnan Province, decisively abandoned his vehicle and switched to taking a high-speed train in Zhaotong due to fatigue and hazardous weather conditions caused by heavy rain, drawing widespread public attention. According to traffic authorities, the man encountered intense rainfall while passing through Zhaotong, resulting in slippery roads and low visibility. After continuous driving for 10 hours, he exhibited clear symptoms of fatigue, including dizziness and impaired concentration. While resting at a service area, to prevent traffic accidents, he voluntarily stopped driving, parked his vehicle, and reported the situation to the police before purchasing a train ticket via his mobile phone to reach his destination. The incident was captured on surveillance footage and uploaded to social media platforms, quickly sparking widespread discussion. Netizens generally praised his "rational choice," noting that under the dual risks of adverse road conditions and physical exhaustion, proactively switching to a safer public transportation mode demonstrated a high degree of responsibility toward personal safety. Data from the Ministry of Public Security show that fatigue-related driving contributes to over 20% of annual traffic accidents, posing a significant safety hazard. Transportation authorities stated they will enhance emergency services and safety warnings at highway service areas, promote intelligent technologies such as "fatigue driving warning systems," and encourage drivers to plan rest breaks appropriately. Railway authorities also responded, affirming their commitment to continuously optimize the high-speed rail network and improve cross-regional transportation connectivity, offering efficient alternatives for unexpected situations during long-distance driving. This incident not only reflects individual safety decision-making under extreme circumstances but also highlights the public's deeper expectations for safer travel options and more human-centered transportation system design.

    [Original] é’±åˆ°åº•è¿˜è¦ä¸è¦å­˜é“¶è¡Œ
    In recent years, the question of whether money still needs to be saved in banks has sparked widespread social debate, reflecting deep public concerns about financial trust and the transformation of savings methods. Data from the central bank show that the growth rate of personal savings deposits slowed significantly in 2023, with some younger groups shifting toward higher-yield channels such as funds, stocks, and digital currencies. This trend stems from multiple overlapping factors. On one hand, bank deposit interest rates have remained persistently low, with some three-year fixed deposits offering annual interest rates below 2%, failing to keep pace with CPI increases and leading to a continuous decline in real purchasing power. On the other hand, internet-based financial platforms such as Yuâ€™ebao and Lingshui Tong have attracted large numbers of post-90s and post-00s users due to their convenience and relatively higher returns. Additionally, although recent failures of some small and medium-sized banks have not undermined the policy foundation of the deposit insurance systemâ€”providing full protection for deposits up to 500,000 yuanâ€”restoring public trust still requires time. Experts point out that banks serve functions far beyond savings; they remain central pillars of economic operations through credit support, payment and settlement services, and wealth management. Faced with competition from internet finance, traditional banks urgently need to achieve transformation through digital upgrades, product optimization, and enhanced service quality. In the future, savings methods will become increasingly diversified. Individuals should reasonably allocate bank deposits, financial products, and physical assets based on their risk tolerance, liquidity needs, and long-term financial planning. Overall, although the "absolute appeal" of bank savings has declined, its role as a critical component of the financial safety net remains irreplaceable. The public should rationally view the evolution of savings, avoiding blind pursuit of high returns while also not completely discarding banks as a stable option, thereby promoting the development of scientific and diversified wealth management strategies.

    [Original] æ˜¥èŠ‚å“ªäº›æ™¯ç‚¹æ›´çƒ­é—¨ï¼Ÿä¸€ç»„æ•°æ®ç›˜ç‚¹
    During the 2024 Spring Festival holiday, China's tourism market reached a peak. According to the latest data from the Data Center of the Ministry of Culture and Tourism, the country is expected to receive over 470 million tourists, a year-on-year increase of approximately 15%, with total tourism revenue projected to exceed 600 billion yuan, setting a new record. Historical and cultural sites, natural scenic areas, and immersive cultural tourism projects have become mainstream, reflecting a deep integration of "culture + tourism." Traditional popular attractions such as the Forbidden City in Beijing, the Terracotta Warriors in Xi'an, West Lake in Hangzhou, Zhangjiajie National Forest Park, and Kuanzhai Alley in Chengdu continue to lead the market. Xi'an, in particular, has once again become the most popular destination nationwide, with its immersive "Tang Dynasty Nocturnal City" performances and Hanfu experience activities attracting over 300,000 visitors per day on average. New cultural tourism landmarks such as Shanghai Disneyland, Guangzhou Chimelong Resort, and Chongqing Hongyadong have also performed strongly, drawing large numbers of young and family tourists through festival events and nighttime economy initiatives. Rural tourism, winter sports tourism, and the "intangible cultural heritage + tourism" model have seen significant growth in popularity. Skiing and ice sculpture projects in Northeast China have drawn strong interest, with Harbin Ice and Snow World receiving over 100,000 visitors per day on average. Meanwhile, destinations such as Lijiang in Yunnan and Qiandongnan in Guizhou have become popular choices for "reverse tourism" due to their unique local customs and ethnic charm, with rural tourism reception increasing by more than 20% year-on-year. Experts point out that the booming tourism market reflects a rebound in residents' consumer confidence and demonstrates the effectiveness of the cultural and tourism industry in product innovation, service upgrading, and digital operations. How to achieve sustainable development while ensuring visitor experience will become a key challenge for cultural and tourism departments across regions in the future.
